قَوْلُهُ ( مَعَ مَلَكَةِ الِاسْتِنْبَاطِ ( أَى الْعِلْمِ بِمَا ذُكِرَ يُشْتَرَطُ كَوْنُهُ مَقْرُونًا بِمَلَكَةِ اسْتِبَاطِ الْفُرُوعِ الْقِيَاسِيَّةِ مِنْ تِلْكَ الْأَحْكَامِ أَوْ اسْتِنْبَاطِ الْأَحْكَامِ مِنْ أَدِلَّتِهَا حَتَّى إنَّ الْعِلْمَ بِالْحُكْمِ بِمُجَرَّدِ سَمَاعِ النَّصَّ لِلْعِلْمِ بِاللُّغَةِ مِنْ غَيْرِ اقْتِدَارٍ عَلَى النَّظَرِ والاستدلال لا يُعَدُّ مِنَ الْفِقْهِ وَالأوَّلُ أَوْجَهُ
ترجمہ:۔ ایسی تعریف ہے جس کو گھڑا گیا ہے فقہ کے لئے اس حیثیت سے کہ منضبط ہو جائیں اس کی معلومات اور قید لگا ناکل احکام کے ساتھ خارج ہو جاتے ہیں اس کے ساتھ بعض احکام مگر بیشک وہ دلالت کرتا ہے اس بات پر کہ بیشک وہ جب ظاہر ہو جائے نزول وحی ایک حکم کے ساتھ یا دو حکموں کے ساتھ پس جاننے والا اس کو ملکہ مذکورہ کے ساتھ نہیں نام رکھا جاتا اس کا فقیہ اور جب جان لے تین احکام کو ( تو ) نام رکھا جاتا ہے فقیہ۔ اور مقید کیا نزول وحی کو ظہور کے ساتھ احتراز کرتے ہوئے ان سے کہ جب نازل ہو اس کے ساتھ وحی اور نہ پہنچے اس (فقیہ) کو پس نہیں ہے فقیہ کی شرط میں سے اس کا پہچاننا۔ قولہ مع ملکۃ الاستنباط: یعنی علم اس چیز کا جن کا پہلے ذکر ہوا اس کیلئے شرط لگائی گئی ہے کہ وہ ملا ہوا ہو فروع قیاسیہ کے استنباط کے ملکہ کیسا تھ ان احکام سے یا احکام کا استنباط کرنے پر ان کی دلیلوں سے یہاں تک کہ بیشک جاننے والا ایک حکم کو صرف سماع نص کے ساتھ بوجہ جاننے لغت کو بغیر قادر ہو نے نظر اور استدلال پر نہیں شمار کیا جا تا فقہ سے اور اول زیادہ بہتر ہے۔ شاریخ کی طرف سے ماتن کی بیان کردہ تعریف پر تبصرہ
تشریح: قولہ بیل ہوا العلم :۔ یہ عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے اس میں شارگے نے ماتن کی بیان کردہ تعریف کی وضاحت کی ہے اور ضرورت بیان کی ہے کہ ماتن کی تعریف کے مطابق فقہ نام ہے ان احکام کا جو وحی سے یا اجماع سے ثابت ہوں اور یہ احکام متناہی ہیں اسی طرح تعریف کے اندر لفظ کل کو ذکر کیا اس سے بعض احکام نکل گئے یعنی کل احکام مراد ہیں لفظ کل کی قید لگانے کی وجہ سے اور اسی طرح مسائل قیاسیہ کو نکالنے کی وجہ سے وہ اعتراض وارد نہیں ہوتے جو ماقبل والی تعریف پر ہوئے تھے۔ الا انہ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے اس سے شاریخ نے ماتن پر اعتراض کیا ہے۔
اعتراض:۔ یہ ہے کہ آپ کی تعریف عجیب ہے کہ اس میں کل احکام کی قید ہے یعنی فقہ تمام احکام کے جانے کا نام ہے احکام یہ جمع ہے اور جمع کا اطلاق کم از کم تین افراد پر ہوتا ہے اب مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ جو تین حکم جانتا ہے یا تین سے زائد حکم جانتا ہے
Answer: According to our definition, fiqh is certain. In our definition, qiyasi issues are not included because in our definition fiqh is knowledge of those rulings which are derived from Quran, Hadith, and Ijma, and all these are certain. Answer (2): Even if we consider it zanni, the application of knowledge is correct because knowledge is also applied to [zanniyat?] such as knowledge of medicine, knowledge of morphology, etc., because these are written by people, they are not revealed from Allah. When knowledge can be applied to [zanniyat?], then calling it 'ilm al-fiqh' is also correct. Answer (3): Even if we include qiyasi issues, fiqh is still certain because the rulings established by qiyas are recognized by Shari'ah. Allah commanded: 'So take heed, O people of insight.' Similarly, the Prophet asked Mu'adh: 'If you do not find a ruling explicitly in Quran and Hadith, what will you do?' He replied: 'I will exercise my own judgment (ijtihad bi ra'yi).' The Prophet prayed for him and did not disapprove. Thus, it is established from the Prophet's tacit approval that qiyasi issues are valid. So it is as if the Lawgiver said: 'Whatever the mujtahid's predominant opinion leads to, the ruling is established with certainty.' This [latter statement] is according to those who consider every mujtahid correct; it is apparent for them. As for those who do not consider every mujtahid correct — and I believe this is the truth — for them this proposition is not valid because if there is an error, it is not established with Allah. So they will interpret 'Whatever the mujtahid's predominant opinion leads to' as: 'It becomes obligatory to act upon it.' When action is obligatory, it is certain. Then upon certainty, action is obligatory for the mujtahid. Therefore, when it is certain from the perspective of Shari'ah, knowledge can be applied to certainties. Or these people will say: 'Whatever the mujtahid's predominant opinion leads to, the ruling is established with respect to the evidence,' meaning rulings established by qiyas are established by considering the evidence, even if they are not established in reality and with Allah. And a ruling established by evidence is also certain. Summary: In fiqh, certain issues are mentioned, therefore knowledge can be applied to it. (And Allah knows best.)
Al-Talwih: His statement: 'Rather it is knowledge' — a contrived definition of fiqh such that its known matters are delimited. The restriction to 'all rulings' excludes some. However, it indicates that when revelation descends with one or two rulings, the one who knows them with the aforementioned faculty is not called a faqih; when he knows three rulings, he is called a faqih. He restricted the descent of revelation to 'apparent' to exclude what has been revealed but has not yet reached him; it is not a condition of the faqih to know it. His statement: 'with a faculty of istinbat' — i.e., knowledge of what has been mentioned is conditioned to be accompanied by a faculty of deriving qiyasi branches from those rulings or deriving rulings from their evidence, such that knowledge of a ruling merely by hearing the text due to knowledge of language without ability to consider and deduce is not considered fiqh. And the first is more appropriate.
Translation: It is a definition that has been coined for fiqh in such a way that its known matters are delimited. The restriction with 'all rulings' excludes some rulings. But it indicates that when revelation becomes apparent with one ruling or two rulings, the knower of it with the aforementioned faculty is not called a faqih; when he knows three rulings, he is called a faqih. He restricted the descent of revelation to 'apparent' to exclude those that have descended but have not yet reached him; it is not part of the condition of the faqih to know it. His statement 'with a faculty of istinbat': meaning knowledge of the things mentioned is conditioned to be accompanied by a faculty of istinbat of qiyasi branches from those rulings or deriving rulings from their evidence, such that the knower of a single ruling merely through hearing the text due to knowledge of language without being able to consider and deduce is not counted from fiqh; and the first is more appropriate. Commentary by the commentator on the definition expressed by the matn.
Explanation: His statement 'Rather it is knowledge': This is the first part of the expression. In this, the commentator explains the definition expressed by the matn and states the need: according to the matn's definition, fiqh is the name of those rulings that are established by revelation or ijma, and these rulings are finite. Similarly, using the word 'all' in the definition excludes some rulings, i.e., all rulings are meant due to the restriction of the word 'all'. And because of excluding qiyasi issues, the objections that were raised against the previous definition do not arise. 'However' — this is the second part of the commentator's expression. Here the commentator objects to the matn. Objection: Your definition is strange because it has the restriction of 'all rulings', i.e., fiqh is the name of knowing all rulings. 'Rulings' is a plural, and plural applies to at least three individuals. So the meaning would be that whoever knows three rulings or more is called a faqih.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
The passage is a definition of fiqh with conditions and responses to objections. It begins with two Urdu answers to objections about the certainty of fiqh: fiqh is certain because it is based on qat'i sources; even if zanni, the term 'knowledge' applies analogously to other fields; and qiyasi rulings are considered certain because Shari'ah has validated them through Quranic command and the Prophet's tacit approval of Mu'adh's ijtihad. The Arabic text from Al-Talwih defines fiqh as a contrived definition that requires knowledge of all rulings, but the plural 'all rulings' implies at least three, so someone knowing one or two rulings is not a faqih. The condition of 'malakat al-istinbat' (faculty of derivation) is added: mere knowledge of language without the ability to deduce is not fiqh. The Urdu commentary explains that the definition excludes qiyasi issues from the previous definition but here they are included, and an objection is noted that defining fiqh as knowledge of all rulings would require knowing at least three rulings, which is problematic. The passage then discusses the two views on whether every mujtahid is correct and concludes that even for those who hold that not every mujtahid is correct, the ruling from qiyas is certain with respect to evidence, thus the term 'knowledge' applies.

Key Terms
الفقه (al-fiqh): Knowledge of all Shar'i rulings derived from Quran, Hadith, Ijma, and Qiyas with a faculty of istinbat
ملكة الاستنباط (malakat al-istinbat): A faculty enabling the derivation of rulings from evidence, including qiyasi branches
الظن (al-zann): Predominant opinion that becomes binding when supported by Shari'ah, thus considered certain in terms of obligation
القطع (al-qat'): Certainty; in this context, a ruling that is binding and beyond doubt for the mujtahid
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning extending a ruling from an established case to a new case due to shared effective cause

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the definition discussed in the passage, how many ahkam must one know to be called a faqih?
A) One or two
B) Exactly three
C) Three or more
D) All rulings without exception

Key Takeaway
Fiqh is certain knowledge because the Shari'ah's validation of qiyas elevates predominant opinion to binding certainty, and the faqih is distinguished by the faculty of deriving branches.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Definition of Fiqh: The Indispensable Faculty of Istinbat
Commentary expanding the definitional condition of istinbat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two components of the Hanafi definition of fiqh and explain why the faculty of istinbat is necessary for being a faqih.

Core Idea
Fiqh is knowledge of rulings with the faculty to derive new rulings—mere memorization is insufficient.

The Hanafi school defines fiqh more strictly than simply knowing rules. In this passage, the commentator expands on the condition 'with the faculty of istinbat,' clarifying that a person who merely memorizes texts without the ability to perform ijtihad is not a faqih. We will examine the definition, an objection, and the commentator's resolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components of the definition
The definition of fiqh consists of two parts: knowledge of rulings from revelation or consensus, and the condition of having the faculty of istinbat. Identify each part in the Arabic text.
The word 'ma'a' indicates accompaniment.
2
Understand why the faculty is required
The commentator explains that knowing a ruling merely by hearing the text (due to language knowledge) without ability for reflection and inference is not fiqh. Reflect on why this distinction matters.
This separates taqlid from ijtihad.
3
Analyze the objection regarding 'all rulings'
An objector argues that if 'all rulings' (al-ahkam kull) means at least three, early Companions with only one or two rulings would not be fuqaha. Follow how the commentator frames this objection and why it is weak.
The objection is hypothetical because the faculty of istinbat requires repeated knowledge, not a fixed number.
4
Examine the two interpretations of 'istinbat'
The phrase 'ma'a malakat al-istinbat' has two possible interpretations: (1) deriving analogical branches from rulings, or (2) deriving rulings from evidences. The commentator favors the first. Compare the two and see why the first is more appropriate.
Fiqh is about applying rulings to new cases, not just extracting them from sources.

احکام اکٹھے اتارے گئے ہوں خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اعتراض فرض محض پر محمول ہے حقیقت پر مبنی نہیں اور اگر تم یہ فرض کر سکتے ہو تو ہم بھی یہ فرض کر سکتے ہیں کہ ابتداء سے ہی بہت سارے مسائل اکٹھے نازل ہوئے تھے۔ وقید نزول الوحی:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے اس عبارت میں متن کی وضاحت ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ متن میں ظہور وحی کی قید لگائی ہے اس کا فائدہ بیان کیا کہ اگر حکم نازل ہوا ہو گر فقیہ پر ظہور نہ ہوا ہو لفظ احکام ہو گا معنی ہوگا کہ وہ علم ملا ہوا ہو ا حکام سے فروع قیاسیہ کے استنباط پر (۲) مضاف الیہ احکام ہوں تو اس صورت میں منہا کی ضمیر کا مرجع لفظ ادلہ ہو گا اب معنی ہوگا وہ علم مقرون ہو دلائل سے احکام کے استنباط پر اب تاریخ نے کہا کہ پہلا احتمال راجح ہے کیونکہ فقہ صرف دلائل سے احکام کے استنباط کا نام نہیں بلکہ احکام سے جزئیات کا استنباط فقہ ہے اور یہ اس وقت ہوگا جب کہ احکام سے فروع قیاسیہ کا استنباط ہو۔
His statement: 'with the faculty of istinbat' – meaning the knowledge of what was mentioned is conditioned upon being accompanied by the faculty of deriving analogical branches from those rulings, or deriving rulings from their evidences, such that knowledge of a ruling merely by hearing the text due to knowledge of language without ability for reflection and inference is not considered fiqh, and the first is more appropriate. Translation: Such a definition is coined for fiqh in the sense that its information is systematized, and the restriction 'all rulings' excludes some rulings, but it indicates that when revelation of one or two rulings becomes manifest, the knower without the aforementioned faculty is not called a faqih, and when he knows three rulings he is called a faqih. And revelation was restricted with manifestation to exclude those cases where revelation occurred but did not reach the faqih, so knowing it is not a condition for being a faqih. His statement: 'with the faculty of istinbat' – i.e., knowledge of what was previously mentioned is conditioned upon being accompanied by the faculty of deriving analogical branches from those rulings or deriving rulings from their evidences, such that one who knows a single ruling merely by hearing the text due to language knowledge without ability for reflection and inference is not counted from fiqh, and the first is more appropriate. Commentary by the commentator on the matan's definition. Explanation: His statement 'with knowledge' – this is the first part of the passage. Here the commentator explains the definition given by the matan and states the need that according to the matan's definition, fiqh is the name of those rulings that are established by revelation or consensus, and these rulings are finite. Similarly, mentioning the word 'all' in the definition excludes some rulings, i.e., 'all rulings' is intended because of the restriction with 'all', and similarly because of deriving analogical issues, the objections that occurred on the previous definition do not arise. However, this is the second part of the commentary's passage – here the commentator objects to the matan. Objection: That your definition is strange because it contains the restriction 'all rulings', meaning fiqh is the name of knowing all rulings. 'Rulings' is plural, and plural applies to at least three. So the meaning would be that one who knows three rulings or more with the correct faculty of istinbat is a faqih; one who knows one or two rulings is not a faqih. This necessitates that as long as three rulings had not been revealed, no Companion was a faqih. So your definition is not free of objection. Answer (1): That 'rulings' is plural, and when the definite article enters the plural, its plurality is nullified, so it applies to the totality of rulings and also to a single ruling. So the meaning would be: every ruling whose manifestation from revelation has occurred, knowing it is fiqh. But this answer is weak because although the definite article breaks the plurality, the word 'all' also enters and it applies to multiple, so we can still intend more than three, not less. Answer (2): The substantive answer is that this objection is based on pure assumption because the definition includes the condition of the correct faculty of istinbat. This faculty is not produced by knowing one or two rulings; it requires repeated knowledge of particulars. And even if we assume that one or two rulings produce the correct faculty of istinbat, then we say it is not necessary that rulings were revealed sequentially; rather it is possible that many rulings were revealed together. In summary, the objection is based on assumption, not reality. And if you can assume, we can also assume that from the beginning many issues were revealed together. And the restriction 'revelation' – this is the last part of the commentary's passage. Here the matan is explained: the matan added the restriction of manifestation of revelation, and its benefit is that if a ruling was revealed but did not become manifest to the faqih, then knowing it is not necessary for the faqih. His statement 'with faculty' – this is the first part of the passage. Here the commentator's purpose is to explain the matan: in the matan, the author's definition had the condition 'with the correct faculty of istinbat'. He explains that the word 'ma'a' is in the meaning of 'accompanied', and the 'al' on 'istinbat' is compensatory, the possessed is omitted, and the 'al' is inserted on the possessor instead. There are two possibilities for the possessed: (1) they are analogical branches – then the pronoun 'minha' refers to 'rulings', meaning that knowledge is accompanied by deriving analogical branches from those rulings. (2) the possessed is rulings – then the pronoun 'minha' refers to 'evidences', meaning that knowledge is accompanied by deriving rulings from evidences. Then al-Tariq said: the first probability is more preponderant because fiqh is not only the deriving of rulings from evidences; rather deriving particulars from rulings is fiqh, and that occurs when analogical branches are derived from rulings.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the definition of fiqh, specifically expanding on the condition of 'malakat al-istinbat' (faculty of correct derivation). The author of the matn defined fiqh as knowledge of rulings from revelation or consensus, with the condition of having the faculty to derive rulings. The commentator explains that simply knowing a ruling by hearing the text without the ability to perform ijtihad is not fiqh. Then an objection is raised: if 'all rulings' means at least three (due to plural minimum), then early Companions who only knew one or two rulings would not be fuqaha. Two answers are given: first, that the definite article on the plural can refer to the genus, so it includes even one ruling, but this is weak because of the word 'kull'. The second, stronger answer is that the objection is hypothetical because the faculty of istinbat is not acquired from one or two rulings; it requires repeated knowledge. Also, it is possible that many rulings were revealed at once. The commentator then discusses the phrase 'with the faculty of istinbat' in detail, analyzing the Arabic grammar and presenting two interpretations: (1) deriving analogical branches from rulings, or (2) deriving rulings from evidences. He favors the first because fiqh is primarily about deriving particular cases from general rulings. The passage is a typical Hanafi usul discussion focusing on the precise definition of fiqh and the necessary conditions for a person to be considered a faqih.

Key Terms
ملکۃ الاستنباط (malakat al-istinbat): The faculty or ability to derive legal rulings from their evidences or to derive analogical branches from primary rulings.
فقہ (fiqh): Knowledge of rulings from revelation or consensus with the condition of having the faculty of istinbat.
الاحکام (al-ahkam): Plural of hukm; here refers to rulings from revelation or consensus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition discussed in this lesson, which of the following best describes a faqih?
A) A person who memorizes all Quranic verses and hadiths.
B) A person who knows rulings from revelation or consensus and has the ability to derive new rulings from them.
C) A person who has studied fiqh books for many years.
D) A person who can recite the Quran with proper tajweed.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh in the Hanafi school is not mere knowledge of texts but knowledge accompanied by the faculty to derive rulings—without this faculty, one is not a faqih.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Fiqh as Knowledge with Faculty of Deduction
Definition of fiqh with condition of malaka

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of fiqh and explain why the condition of malakat al-istinbat is essential, distinguishing it from mere knowledge of rulings.

Core Idea
Fiqh is not just knowing rulings; it is having the faculty to deduce them.

This passage from a commentary on usul al-fiqh carefully unpacks the definition of fiqh. The author defines fiqh as knowledge of revealed rulings coupled with a faculty for correct deduction. A key objection—that early Companions would not be fuqaha because they knew few rulings—is addressed, ultimately highlighting the centrality of the faculty (malaka) and the progressive nature of revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition’s components
Locate the two conditions in the definition: (1) knowledge of rulings that have been manifested through revelation (zuhur al-wahi), and (2) the faculty of correct deduction (malakat al-istinbat).
The commentary explains that 'ma'a malaka' means the knowledge is accompanied by this faculty.
2
Analyze the objection based on few rulings
The objection states: if fiqh requires knowledge of multiple rulings (because 'ahkam' is plural), then early Companions who knew only one or two rulings were not fuqaha. Understand why this challenges the definition.
The objection uses the word 'kull' to imply at least three.
3
Evaluate the first answer
The first answer argues that alif lam on a plural can refer to a single instance, so 'ahkam' could mean a single ruling. Why is this considered weak?
Because 'kull' still implies multiplicity, so the plural sense remains.
4
Evaluate the second answer
The stronger answer invokes the condition of malaka: the faculty is not developed from one or two rulings; it requires repeated exposure. Also, multiple rulings could have been revealed together from the start.
This shifts the focus from quantity of rulings to the quality of deductive ability.
5
Distinguish between static and dynamic fiqh
Contrast the conventional view of fiqh as a fixed science with the author’s view: fiqh is a universal concept that expands over time as new cases arise.
This has implications for who is considered a faqih across different eras.

استنباط صحیح کے ملکہ کے ساتھ وہ فقیہ ہے جو ایک حکم یا دو حکم کو جانتا ہو وہ فقیہ نہ ہوا اب یہ لازم آیا جب تک تین حکم نازل نہ ہوئے تھے اس وقت تک کوئی صحابی فقیہ نہ تھا تو آپ کی تعریف بھی خالی از اعتراض نہ رہی۔
جواب (۱):- یہ ہے کہ احکام جمع ہے اور جب جمع پر الف لام داخل ہو تو اسکی جمعیت باطل ہو جاتی ہے تو اب یہ احکام کے مجموعہ پر بھی اور ایک حکم پر بھی صادق آئے گا اب معنی ہوگا ہر وہ حکم جس کا ظہور نزول وحی سے ہو چکا ہو اس کے جاننے کا نام فقہ ہے لیکن یہ جواب کمزور ہے کیونکہ اگر چہ جمع پر الف لام داخل ہو تو اس کی جمعیت ٹوٹ جاتی ہے لیکن لفظ کل بھی داخل ہے اور یہ متعدد پر داخل ہوتا ہے لہذا اب بھی تین احکام سے زائد مراد لے سکتے ہیں کم نہیں۔
جواب (۲): تحقیقی جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ اعتراض صرف فرض محض پر مبنی ہے اس لئے کہ تعریف میں استنباط صحیح کے ملکہ کی قید ہے یہ ملکہ ایک حکم یا دو حکم معلوم کرنے سے پیدا نہیں ہوتا جب تک جزئیات کا علم بار بار حاصل نہ ہو اور اگر مان بھی لیں کہ ایک دو حکم سے استنباط صحیح کا ملکہ حاصل ہو جاتا ہے تو پھر ہم کہیں گے کہ یہ بھی ضروری نہیں کہ احکام ترتیب وار نازل ہوئے ہیں بلکہ ایسے ہو سکتا ہے کہ کئی احکام اکٹھے اتارے گئے ہوں خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اعتراض فرض محض پر محمول ہے حقیقت پر مبنی نہیں اور اگر تم یہ فرض کر سکتے ہو تو ہم بھی یہ فرض کر سکتے ہیں کہ ابتداء سے ہی بہت سارے مسائل اکٹھے نازل ہوئے تھے۔
وقید نزول الوحی:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے اس عبارت میں متن کی وضاحت ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ متن میں ظہور وحی کی قید لگائی ہے اس کا فائدہ بیان کیا کہ اگر حکم نازل ہوا ہو گر فقیہ پر ظہور نہ ہوا ہو تو اس کا جاننا فقیہ کے لئے ضروری نہیں ہے۔ قوله مع ملکہ :۔ یہ عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے اس میں غرض شاریخ وضاحت متن ہے متن کے اندر مصنف کی تعریف میں قید تھی مع ملکہ الاستنباط اصیح اس کی وضاحت کی ہے کہ لفظ مع مقرون کے معنی میں ہے اور استنباط پر الف لام عوض کا ہے مضاف الیہ محذوف ہے اس کے بدلے مضاف پر الف لام داخل کیا گیا ہے اور مضاف الیہ میں دو احتمال ہیں (۱) فروع قیاسیہ ہوں اس صورت میں منہا کی ضمیر کا مرجع لفظ احکام ہو گا معنی ہوگا کہ وہ علم ملا ہوا ہو ا حکام سے فروع قیاسیہ کے استنباط پر (۲) مضاف الیہ احکام ہوں تو اس صورت میں منہا کی ضمیر کا مرجع لفظ ادلہ ہو گا اب معنی ہوگا وہ علم مقرون ہو دلائل سے احکام کے استنباط پر اب تاریخ نے کہا کہ پہلا احتمال راجح ہے کیونکہ فقہ صرف دلائل سے احکام کے استنباط کا نام نہیں بلکہ احکام سے جزئیات کا استنباط فقہ ہے اور یہ اس وقت ہوگا جب کہ احکام سے فروع قیاسیہ کا استنباط ہو۔
حتی ان العلم :۔ یہ عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے اس میں شاریخ نے مع ملکہ والی قید کا فائدہ بیان کیا ہے کہ اگر کسی کو لغت کے زور پر مسئلہ معلوم ہو جائے اس کو فقیہ نہیں کہیں گے جب تک استنباط کا ملکہ اور استعداد پیدا نہ ہو۔ قَوْلُهُ ) لَا الْمَسَائِلُ الْقِيَاسِيَّةُ ) أَى لَا يُشْتَرَطُ فِي الْفِقْهِ الْعِلْمُ بِالْمَسَائِل الْقِيَاسِيَّةِ ؛ لأنَّهَا نَتِيجَةُ الْفَقَاهَةِ وَالاجْتِهَادِ لِكَوْنِهَا فُرُوعًا مُسْتَتْبَطَةٌ بِالِاجْتِهَادِ فَيَتَوَقَّفُ الْعِلْمُ بِهَا عَلَى كَوْنِ الشَّخْصِ فَقِيهَا فَلَوْ تَوَقَّفَتِ الْفَقَاهَةُ عَلَيْهَا لَزِمَ الدَّوُرُ ، فَإِنْ قِيلَ هَذَا إِنَّمَا يَسْتَقِيمُ فِى أَوَّلِ الْقَائِسِينَ . وَأَمَّا مَنْ بَعْدَهُ فَيَجُوزُ أَن يُشْتَرَطَ فِيهِ الْعِلْمُ بِالْمَسَائِلِ الْقِيَاسِيَّةِ الَّتِي اسْتَنْبَطَهَا الْمُجْتَهِدُ الْأَوَّلُ مِنْ غَيْرِ لُزُومِ دَوْرٍ قُلْنَا لَا يَجُوزُ لِلْمُجْتَهِدِ التَّقْلِيدُ ، بَلْ يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَعْرِفَ الْمَسَائِلَ الْقِيَاسِيَّةِ بِاجْتِهَادِهِ فَلَوْ اُشْتَرِطَ الْعِلْمُ بِهَا لَزِمَ الدَّوْرُ نَعَمُ يُشْتَرَطُ أَنْ يَعْرِفَ أَقْوَالَ الْمُجْتَهِدِينَ فِي الْمَسَائِلِ الْقِيَاسِيَّةِ لِئَلَّا يَقَعَ فِى مُخَالَفَةِ الْإِجْمَاعِ ، فَإِنْ قِيلَ الْمَسَائِلُ الْقِيَاسِيَّةُ مِمَّا ظَهَرَ نُزُولُ الْوَحى بها ، إذ القِيَاسُ مُظْهِرُ لَا مُثْبِتْ فَيُشْتَرَطُ لِلْمُجْتَهِدِ الْأَخِيرِ الْعِلْمُ بِهَا قُلْنَا نُزُولُ الْوَحْيِ بِهَا إِنَّمَا ظَهَرَ لِلْمُجْتَهِدِ السَّابِقِ لَا فِي الْوَاقِعِ وَلَا عِنْدَ الْمُجْتَهِدِ الثَّانِي وَلَيْسَ لَهُ تَقْلِيدُ الْأَوَّلِ فَلا يُشْتَرَطُ لَهُ مَعْرِفَتُهُ وَيُمْكِنُ أَنْ يُرَادَ مَا ظَهَرَ نُزُولُ الْوَحْيِ بِهِ لَا بِتُوَسُطِ الْقِيَاسِ ، ثُمَّ هَهُنَا أَبْحَاتُ الْأَوَّلُ أَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ تَعْرِيفُ الْفِقْهِ الْمُصْطَلَحٍ بَيْنَ الْقَوْمِ ، وَهُوَ عِنْدَهُمُ اسْمٌ لِعِلْمٍ مَخْصُوصِ مُعَيَّنٍ كَسَائِرِ الْعُلُومِ وَعَلَى مَا ذَكَرَهُ الْمُصَنِّفُ هُوَ اسْمٌ لِمَفْهُومٍ كُلِّى يَتَبَدَّلُ بِحَسَبِ الْأَيَّامِ وَالْأَعْصَارِ فَيَوْمًا يَكُونُ عِلْمًا بِجُمْلَةٍ مِنْ الْأَحْكَامِ وَيَوْمًا بِأَكْثَرَ وَأَكْثَرَ وَهَكَذَا يَتَزَايَدُ إِلَى انُقِرَاضِ زَمَنِ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ ، ثُمَّ أَخَذَ يَتَزَايَدُ بِحَسَبِ الْأَعْصَارِ وَانْعِقَادِ الْإِجْمَاعَاتِ وَأَيْضًا يَنتَقِصُ بِحَسَبِ النَّوَاسِخِ وَالْإِجْمَاعِ عَلَى خِلَافِ أَخْبَارِ الْآحَادِ الثَّانِي أَنَّ التَّعْرِيفَ لَا يَصْدُقُ عَلَى فِقْهِ الصَّحَابَةِ فِي زَمَنِ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ
A person who knows one or two rulings with the faculty of correct deduction is not a faqih. This necessitates that as long as three rulings had not been revealed, no Companion was a faqih, so your definition is not free from objection. Answer (1): It is that 'ahkam' is plural, and when alif lam enters on a plural, its plurality becomes invalid, so it applies to a totality of rulings and also to a single ruling. Now the meaning is: every ruling whose revelation has become manifest, knowing it is fiqh. But this answer is weak, because although alif lam breaks the plurality, the word 'kull' is also present, and it enters upon multiples, so we can still intend more than three rulings, not less. Answer (2): The research answer is that this objection is based only on pure assumption, because in the definition there is the condition of 'ma'a malakat al-istinbat al-sahih'. This faculty is not produced by knowing one or two rulings until knowledge of particulars is obtained repeatedly. Even if we accept that the faculty of correct deduction is acquired from one or two rulings, then we would say that it is not necessary that rulings were revealed consecutively; rather it is possible that several rulings were revealed together. In summary, the objection is based on pure assumption, not reality. And if you can assume this, we can also assume that from the beginning many issues were revealed together. And the condition of 'zuhur al-wahi': This is the last part of the commentary's expression. In this expression there is clarification of the matn, the summary of which is that in the matn the condition of manifestation of revelation is placed. Its benefit is stated: if a ruling has been revealed but has not been manifested to the faqih, then knowing it is not necessary for the faqih. His saying 'ma'a malakat': This is the first part of the expression. Here the commentator's purpose is to clarify the matn. In the matn the author's definition had the condition 'ma'a malakat al-istinbat al-sahih'. He clarifies that the word 'ma'a' is in the sense of 'with', and the alif lam on 'istinbat' is compensatory; the mudaf ilayhi is omitted, and in its place the alif lam is inserted on the mudaf. There are two possibilities for the mudaf ilayhi: (1) it is qiyasi furu'; in that case the referent of the pronoun 'minha' is the word 'ahkam', meaning: that knowledge is accompanied with the deduction of qiyasi branches from rulings. (2) The mudaf ilayhi is 'ahkam'; in that case the referent of 'minha' is 'adillah', meaning: that knowledge is accompanied with the deduction of rulings from evidences. The author said that the first probability is preponderant, because fiqh is not merely the deduction of rulings from evidences, but rather the deduction of particulars from rulings is fiqh, and that occurs when there is deduction of qiyasi branches from rulings. 'Hatta inna al-'ilm': This is the second part of the expression. In it the commentator states the benefit of the condition of 'ma'a al-malaka': that if someone knows an issue by force of language, he will not be called a faqih until the faculty and aptitude for deduction is produced. His saying: 'la al-masa'il al-qiyasiyya' means: knowledge of qiyasi issues is not a condition in fiqh, because they are the result of fiqh and ijtihad, since they are branches deduced by ijtihad. Thus knowledge of them depends on the person being a faqih; if fiqh were dependent on them, circularity would result. If it is said: This is valid only for the first of those who perform qiyas. As for after him, it is permissible to condition knowledge of the qiyasi issues that the first mujtahid deduced without circularity. We say: Taqlid is not permissible for a mujtahid; rather he must know the qiyasi issues by his own ijtihad. So if knowledge of them were conditioned, circularity would still result. Yes, he is required to know the statements of the mujtahids regarding qiyasi issues, lest he fall into violation of consensus. If it is said: The qiyasi issues are among those for which the revelation's descent has become manifest, because qiyas is a manifester, not an establisher, so for the later mujtahid knowledge of them is required. We say: The descent of revelation regarding them became manifest only for the earlier mujtahid, not in reality nor for the second mujtahid, and he cannot follow the first, so knowledge of them is not required for him. It is also possible that what is meant is that which the revelation's descent has become manifest without the intermediary of qiyas. Then here are investigations: The first: That what is intended is the definition of fiqh as a technical term among the people (scholars). According to them it is a name for a specific, particular science like other sciences. But according to what the author mentioned, it is a name for a universal concept that changes according to days and eras. One day it is knowledge of a certain sum of rulings, another day more and more, and so it increases until the end of the Prophet's time (peace be upon him). Then it continued to increase according to eras and the formation of consensus, and also decreases according to abrogations and consensus contrary to ahad reports. The second: That the definition does not apply to the fiqh of the Companions during the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the definition of fiqh. The author (Mulla Jalal al-Din al-Tawdihi?) had defined fiqh as knowledge of the rulings of Islamic law that have been manifested through revelation, coupled with the faculty (malaka) of correct deduction (istinbat). The commentator here clarifies and defends this definition. He first addresses an objection: if fiqh requires knowing multiple rulings, then the early Companions who knew only one or two rulings would not be fuqaha. He gives two answers. The first answer attempts to argue that the plural 'ahkam' with alif lam can refer to a single ruling, but that is weak because the word 'kull' implies multitude. The second, stronger answer is that the definition includes the faculty of deduction, which is not acquired from just one or two rulings; it requires repeated exposure. Moreover, it is possible that multiple rulings were revealed together from the start. The commentator then explains the phrase 'qayd nuzul al-wahi' (condition of revelation's manifestation): a ruling that has been revealed but not yet manifested to a faqih need not be known for him to be considered a faqih. Next, he dissects 'ma'a malakat' (with faculty): 'ma'a' means 'accompanied by', and the alif lam on 'istinbat' is compensatory for a missing mudaf ilayhi. He presents two possible referents: the faculty is knowledge of how to deduce qiyasi branches from rulings (first probability) or knowledge of how to deduce rulings from evidences (second probability). He favors the first because fiqh is not just deduction from evidences but rather deriving particulars from general rulings. Then he discusses the benefit of the condition: someone who knows rulings by rote (e.g., from language) is not a faqih unless he has the faculty of deduction. Continuing, the text addresses the issue of qiyasi issues (masa'il qiyasiyya). These are analogical rulings derived from primary sources. They are the result of fiqh, so knowledge of them cannot be a prerequisite for fiqh, or else there would be circularity. An objection is raised: this applies only to the first mujtahid; later mujtahids could be required to know the qiyasi issues deduced by earlier ones without circularity. The commentator responds that a mujtahid cannot do taqlid; he must derive them again. Therefore, requiring knowledge of those specific issues would still create a circular dependency (since to be a mujtahid he must deduce them, but to deduce them he must already be a mujtahid). However, he is required to know the previous mujtahids' positions to avoid violating consensus. Another objection: since qiyas only manifests what is already in revelation, the later mujtahid should know those manifested rulings. The answer distinguishes between manifestation for the first mujtahid (who established the analogy) and for the second (who does not see that revelation directly). The second mujtahid cannot simply follow the first. Finally, the commentator offers two research points: (1) The author's definition treats fiqh as a changing concept, increasing in scope over time, whereas the conventional definition among scholars treats it as a fixed science. (2) The definition does not apply to the fiqh of the Companions during the Prophet's time because they obtained rulings directly from revelation without the need for the faculty of deduction. This passage is essential for understanding the Hanafi epistemological view of fiqh as a dynamic process of deduction rather than static knowledge.

Key Terms
فقہ (fiqh): Knowledge of the rulings of Islamic law that have been manifested through revelation, coupled with the faculty of correct deduction (istinbat).
ملکۃ الاستنباط (malakat al-istinbat): The entrenched faculty or ability in a person that enables him to derive legal rulings from their sources (Quran, Sunnah, etc.) with accuracy.
ظہور الوحی (zuhur al-wahi): The manifestation of revelation to the faqih: a ruling is considered manifest when it has been communicated to the faqih through valid means (Quran, hadith).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, why is the first answer to the objection (that alif lam on a plural can refer to a single) considered weak?
A) Because the alif lam does not break the plurality at all.
B) Because the word 'kull' (all) is also present and implies multiplicity.
C) Because the objection was about the number of rulings, not the definition.
D) Because the first answer contradicts the Hanafi school.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh is not static knowledge but a dynamic faculty of deduction from revealed sources.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

8 min
Qiyasi Issues and Circularity in Defining Fiqh
Why qiyasi issues are not a condition for fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why qiyasi issues cannot be a prerequisite for fiqh according to the Hanafi school, using the concept of circularity (dawr) and the prohibition of taqlid for the mujtahid.

Core Idea
Qiyasi issues are the outcome of fiqh, not its condition; requiring them would create a vicious circle.

This passage continues the commentary by addressing a crucial question: should the definition of fiqh include knowledge of rulings derived through analogical reasoning (qiyas)? The commentator argues that doing so would lead to logical circularity, and even for later mujtahids, taqlid is not permitted, so they must derive these issues themselves. This reinforces that fiqh is a faculty, not a checklist of rulings.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim about qiyasi issues
The text states: 'la al-masa'il al-qiyasiyya' - knowledge of qiyasi issues is not a condition for fiqh. Why? Because they are the result (natiija) of fiqh and ijtihad.
Qiyasi issues are branches derived from primary rulings by ijtihad.
2
Identify the circularity argument
If fiqh required knowledge of qiyasi issues, then to be a faqih one must know them, but to know them one must already be a faqih (since they are deduced by ijtihad). This is circular (dawr).
The circle: fiqh depends on qiyasi issues, qiyasi issues depend on fiqh.
3
Evaluate the objection regarding later mujtahids
An objector says the circularity only applies to the first generation; later mujtahids could be required to know the qiyasi issues deduced earlier without circularity.
But the commentator responds that a later mujtahid cannot do taqlid; he must deduce them again, so the circle persists.
4
Consider the manifestation of revelation
Another objection: qiyas only manifests what is already in revelation, so qiyasi issues are among what 'has been manifested' and thus should be required.
The response: manifestation occurred for the first mujtahid, not for later ones; the second mujtahid does not see the revelation directly.
5
Recognize the requirement to avoid consensus violation
Although not required to know the exact qiyasi issues, a mujtahid must know the positions of earlier mujtahids to ensure he does not contradict consensus.
This is a separate requirement, not part of the definition of fiqh itself.

Source Text

استنباط صحیح کے ملکہ کے ساتھ وہ فقیہ ہے جو ایک حکم یا دو حکم کو جانتا ہو وہ فقیہ نہ ہوا اب یہ لازم آیا جب تک تین حکم نازل نہ ہوئے تھے اس وقت تک کوئی صحابی فقیہ نہ تھا تو آپ کی تعریف بھی خالی از اعتراض نہ رہی۔
جواب (۱):- یہ ہے کہ احکام جمع ہے اور جب جمع پر الف لام داخل ہو تو اسکی جمعیت باطل ہو جاتی ہے تو اب یہ احکام کے مجموعہ پر بھی اور ایک حکم پر بھی صادق آئے گا اب معنی ہوگا ہر وہ حکم جس کا ظہور نزول وحی سے ہو چکا ہو اس کے جاننے کا نام فقہ ہے لیکن یہ جواب کمزور ہے کیونکہ اگر چہ جمع پر الف لام داخل ہو تو اس کی جمعیت ٹوٹ جاتی ہے لیکن لفظ کل بھی داخل ہے اور یہ متعدد پر داخل ہوتا ہے لہذا اب بھی تین احکام سے زائد مراد لے سکتے ہیں کم نہیں۔
جواب (۲): تحقیقی جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ اعتراض صرف فرض محض پر مبنی ہے اس لئے کہ تعریف میں استنباط صحیح کے ملکہ کی قید ہے یہ ملکہ ایک حکم یا دو حکم معلوم کرنے سے پیدا نہیں ہوتا جب تک جزئیات کا علم بار بار حاصل نہ ہو اور اگر مان بھی لیں کہ ایک دو حکم سے استنباط صحیح کا ملکہ حاصل ہو جاتا ہے تو پھر ہم کہیں گے کہ یہ بھی ضروری نہیں کہ احکام ترتیب وار نازل ہوئے ہیں بلکہ ایسے ہو سکتا ہے کہ کئی احکام اکٹھے اتارے گئے ہوں خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اعتراض فرض محض پر محمول ہے حقیقت پر مبنی نہیں اور اگر تم یہ فرض کر سکتے ہو تو ہم بھی یہ فرض کر سکتے ہیں کہ ابتداء سے ہی بہت سارے مسائل اکٹھے نازل ہوئے تھے۔
وقید نزول الوحی:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے اس عبارت میں متن کی وضاحت ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ متن میں ظہور وحی کی قید لگائی ہے اس کا فائدہ بیان کیا کہ اگر حکم نازل ہوا ہو گر فقیہ پر ظہور نہ ہوا ہو تو اس کا جاننا فقیہ کے لئے ضروری نہیں ہے۔ قوله مع ملکہ :۔ یہ عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے اس میں غرض شاریخ وضاحت متن ہے متن کے اندر مصنف کی تعریف میں قید تھی مع ملکہ الاستنباط اصیح اس کی وضاحت کی ہے کہ لفظ مع مقرون کے معنی میں ہے اور استنباط پر الف لام عوض کا ہے مضاف الیہ محذوف ہے اس کے بدلے مضاف پر الف لام داخل کیا گیا ہے اور مضاف الیہ میں دو احتمال ہیں (۱) فروع قیاسیہ ہوں اس صورت میں منہا کی ضمیر کا مرجع لفظ احکام ہو گا معنی ہوگا کہ وہ علم ملا ہوا ہو ا حکام سے فروع قیاسیہ کے استنباط پر (۲) مضاف الیہ احکام ہوں تو اس صورت میں منہا کی ضمیر کا مرجع لفظ ادلہ ہو گا اب معنی ہوگا وہ علم مقرون ہو دلائل سے احکام کے استنباط پر اب تاریخ نے کہا کہ پہلا احتمال راجح ہے کیونکہ فقہ صرف دلائل سے احکام کے استنباط کا نام نہیں بلکہ احکام سے جزئیات کا استنباط فقہ ہے اور یہ اس وقت ہوگا جب کہ احکام سے فروع قیاسیہ کا استنباط ہو۔
حتی ان العلم :۔ یہ عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے اس میں شاریخ نے مع ملکہ والی قید کا فائدہ بیان کیا ہے کہ اگر کسی کو لغت کے زور پر مسئلہ معلوم ہو جائے اس کو فقیہ نہیں کہیں گے جب تک استنباط کا ملکہ اور استعداد پیدا نہ ہو۔ قَوْلُهُ ) لَا الْمَسَائِلُ الْقِيَاسِيَّةُ ) أَى لَا يُشْتَرَطُ فِي الْفِقْهِ الْعِلْمُ بِالْمَسَائِل الْقِيَاسِيَّةِ ؛ لأنَّهَا نَتِيجَةُ الْفَقَاهَةِ وَالاجْتِهَادِ لِكَوْنِهَا فُرُوعًا مُسْتَتْبَطَةٌ بِالِاجْتِهَادِ فَيَتَوَقَّفُ الْعِلْمُ بِهَا عَلَى كَوْنِ الشَّخْصِ فَقِيهَا فَلَوْ تَوَقَّفَتِ الْفَقَاهَةُ عَلَيْهَا لَزِمَ الدَّوُرُ ، فَإِنْ قِيلَ هَذَا إِنَّمَا يَسْتَقِيمُ فِى أَوَّلِ الْقَائِسِينَ . وَأَمَّا مَنْ بَعْدَهُ فَيَجُوزُ أَن يُشْتَرَطَ فِيهِ الْعِلْمُ بِالْمَسَائِلِ الْقِيَاسِيَّةِ الَّتِي اسْتَنْبَطَهَا الْمُجْتَهِدُ الْأَوَّلُ مِنْ غَيْرِ لُزُومِ دَوْرٍ قُلْنَا لَا يَجُوزُ لِلْمُجْتَهِدِ التَّقْلِيدُ ، بَلْ يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَعْرِفَ الْمَسَائِلَ الْقِيَاسِيَّةِ بِاجْتِهَادِهِ فَلَوْ اُشْتَرِطَ الْعِلْمُ بِهَا لَزِمَ الدَّوْرُ نَعَمُ يُشْتَرَطُ أَنْ يَعْرِفَ أَقْوَالَ الْمُجْتَهِدِينَ فِي الْمَسَائِلِ الْقِيَاسِيَّةِ لِئَلَّا يَقَعَ فِى مُخَالَفَةِ الْإِجْمَاعِ ، فَإِنْ قِيلَ الْمَسَائِلُ الْقِيَاسِيَّةُ مِمَّا ظَهَرَ نُزُولُ الْوَحى بها ، إذ القِيَاسُ مُظْهِرُ لَا مُثْبِتْ فَيُشْتَرَطُ لِلْمُجْتَهِدِ الْأَخِيرِ الْعِلْمُ بِهَا قُلْنَا نُزُولُ الْوَحْيِ بِهَا إِنَّمَا ظَهَرَ لِلْمُجْتَهِدِ السَّابِقِ لَا فِي الْوَاقِعِ وَلَا عِنْدَ الْمُجْتَهِدِ الثَّانِي وَلَيْسَ لَهُ تَقْلِيدُ الْأَوَّلِ فَلا يُشْتَرَطُ لَهُ مَعْرِفَتُهُ وَيُمْكِنُ أَنْ يُرَادَ مَا ظَهَرَ نُزُولُ الْوَحْيِ بِهِ لَا بِتُوَسُطِ الْقِيَاسِ ، ثُمَّ هَهُنَا أَبْحَاتُ الْأَوَّلُ أَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ تَعْرِيفُ الْفِقْهِ الْمُصْطَلَحٍ بَيْنَ الْقَوْمِ ، وَهُوَ عِنْدَهُمُ اسْمٌ لِعِلْمٍ مَخْصُوصِ مُعَيَّنٍ كَسَائِرِ الْعُلُومِ وَعَلَى مَا ذَكَرَهُ الْمُصَنِّفُ هُوَ اسْمٌ لِمَفْهُومٍ كُلِّى يَتَبَدَّلُ بِحَسَبِ الْأَيَّامِ وَالْأَعْصَارِ فَيَوْمًا يَكُونُ عِلْمًا بِجُمْلَةٍ مِنْ الْأَحْكَامِ وَيَوْمًا بِأَكْثَرَ وَأَكْثَرَ وَهَكَذَا يَتَزَايَدُ إِلَى انُقِرَاضِ زَمَنِ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ ، ثُمَّ أَخَذَ يَتَزَايَدُ بِحَسَبِ الْأَعْصَارِ وَانْعِقَادِ الْإِجْمَاعَاتِ وَأَيْضًا يَنتَقِصُ بِحَسَبِ النَّوَاسِخِ وَالْإِجْمَاعِ عَلَى خِلَافِ أَخْبَارِ الْآحَادِ الثَّانِي أَنَّ التَّعْرِيفَ لَا يَصْدُقُ عَلَى فِقْهِ الصَّحَابَةِ فِي زَمَنِ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ
A person who knows one or two rulings with the faculty of correct deduction is not a faqih. This necessitates that as long as three rulings had not been revealed, no Companion was a faqih, so your definition is not free from objection. Answer (1): It is that 'ahkam' is plural, and when alif lam enters on a plural, its plurality becomes invalid, so it applies to a totality of rulings and also to a single ruling. Now the meaning is: every ruling whose revelation has become manifest, knowing it is fiqh. But this answer is weak, because although alif lam breaks the plurality, the word 'kull' is also present, and it enters upon multiples, so we can still intend more than three rulings, not less. Answer (2): The research answer is that this objection is based only on pure assumption, because in the definition there is the condition of 'ma'a malakat al-istinbat al-sahih'. This faculty is not produced by knowing one or two rulings until knowledge of particulars is obtained repeatedly. Even if we accept that the faculty of correct deduction is acquired from one or two rulings, then we would say that it is not necessary that rulings were revealed consecutively; rather it is possible that several rulings were revealed together. In summary, the objection is based on pure assumption, not reality. And if you can assume this, we can also assume that from the beginning many issues were revealed together. And the condition of 'zuhur al-wahi': This is the last part of the commentary's expression. In this expression there is clarification of the matn, the summary of which is that in the matn the condition of manifestation of revelation is placed. Its benefit is stated: if a ruling has been revealed but has not been manifested to the faqih, then knowing it is not necessary for the faqih. His saying 'ma'a malakat': This is the first part of the expression. Here the commentator's purpose is to clarify the matn. In the matn the author's definition had the condition 'ma'a malakat al-istinbat al-sahih'. He clarifies that the word 'ma'a' is in the sense of 'with', and the alif lam on 'istinbat' is compensatory; the mudaf ilayhi is omitted, and in its place the alif lam is inserted on the mudaf. There are two possibilities for the mudaf ilayhi: (1) it is qiyasi furu'; in that case the referent of the pronoun 'minha' is the word 'ahkam', meaning: that knowledge is accompanied with the deduction of qiyasi branches from rulings. (2) The mudaf ilayhi is 'ahkam'; in that case the referent of 'minha' is 'adillah', meaning: that knowledge is accompanied with the deduction of rulings from evidences. The author said that the first probability is preponderant, because fiqh is not merely the deduction of rulings from evidences, but rather the deduction of particulars from rulings is fiqh, and that occurs when there is deduction of qiyasi branches from rulings. 'Hatta inna al-'ilm': This is the second part of the expression. In it the commentator states the benefit of the condition of 'ma'a al-malaka': that if someone knows an issue by force of language, he will not be called a faqih until the faculty and aptitude for deduction is produced. His saying: 'la al-masa'il al-qiyasiyya' means: knowledge of qiyasi issues is not a condition in fiqh, because they are the result of fiqh and ijtihad, since they are branches deduced by ijtihad. Thus knowledge of them depends on the person being a faqih; if fiqh were dependent on them, circularity would result. If it is said: This is valid only for the first of those who perform qiyas. As for after him, it is permissible to condition knowledge of the qiyasi issues that the first mujtahid deduced without circularity. We say: Taqlid is not permissible for a mujtahid; rather he must know the qiyasi issues by his own ijtihad. So if knowledge of them were conditioned, circularity would still result. Yes, he is required to know the statements of the mujtahids regarding qiyasi issues, lest he fall into violation of consensus. If it is said: The qiyasi issues are among those for which the revelation's descent has become manifest, because qiyas is a manifester, not an establisher, so for the later mujtahid knowledge of them is required. We say: The descent of revelation regarding them became manifest only for the earlier mujtahid, not in reality nor for the second mujtahid, and he cannot follow the first, so knowledge of them is not required for him. It is also possible that what is meant is that which the revelation's descent has become manifest without the intermediary of qiyas. Then here are investigations: The first: That what is intended is the definition of fiqh as a technical term among the people (scholars). According to them it is a name for a specific, particular science like other sciences. But according to what the author mentioned, it is a name for a universal concept that changes according to days and eras. One day it is knowledge of a certain sum of rulings, another day more and more, and so it increases until the end of the Prophet's time (peace be upon him). Then it continued to increase according to eras and the formation of consensus, and also decreases according to abrogations and consensus contrary to ahad reports. The second: That the definition does not apply to the fiqh of the Companions during the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the definition of fiqh. The author (Mulla Jalal al-Din al-Tawdihi?) had defined fiqh as knowledge of the rulings of Islamic law that have been manifested through revelation, coupled with the faculty (malaka) of correct deduction (istinbat). The commentator here clarifies and defends this definition. He first addresses an objection: if fiqh requires knowing multiple rulings, then the early Companions who knew only one or two rulings would not be fuqaha. He gives two answers. The first answer attempts to argue that the plural 'ahkam' with alif lam can refer to a single ruling, but that is weak because the word 'kull' implies multitude. The second, stronger answer is that the definition includes the faculty of deduction, which is not acquired from just one or two rulings; it requires repeated exposure. Moreover, it is possible that multiple rulings were revealed together from the start. The commentator then explains the phrase 'qayd nuzul al-wahi' (condition of revelation's manifestation): a ruling that has been revealed but not yet manifested to a faqih need not be known for him to be considered a faqih. Next, he dissects 'ma'a malakat' (with faculty): 'ma'a' means 'accompanied by', and the alif lam on 'istinbat' is compensatory for a missing mudaf ilayhi. He presents two possible referents: the faculty is knowledge of how to deduce qiyasi branches from rulings (first probability) or knowledge of how to deduce rulings from evidences (second probability). He favors the first because fiqh is not just deduction from evidences but rather deriving particulars from general rulings. Then he discusses the benefit of the condition: someone who knows rulings by rote (e.g., from language) is not a faqih unless he has the faculty of deduction. Continuing, the text addresses the issue of qiyasi issues (masa'il qiyasiyya). These are analogical rulings derived from primary sources. They are the result of fiqh, so knowledge of them cannot be a prerequisite for fiqh, or else there would be circularity. An objection is raised: this applies only to the first mujtahid; later mujtahids could be required to know the qiyasi issues deduced by earlier ones without circularity. The commentator responds that a mujtahid cannot do taqlid; he must derive them again. Therefore, requiring knowledge of those specific issues would still create a circular dependency (since to be a mujtahid he must deduce them, but to deduce them he must already be a mujtahid). However, he is required to know the previous mujtahids' positions to avoid violating consensus. Another objection: since qiyas only manifests what is already in revelation, the later mujtahid should know those manifested rulings. The answer distinguishes between manifestation for the first mujtahid (who established the analogy) and for the second (who does not see that revelation directly). The second mujtahid cannot simply follow the first. Finally, the commentator offers two research points: (1) The author's definition treats fiqh as a changing concept, increasing in scope over time, whereas the conventional definition among scholars treats it as a fixed science. (2) The definition does not apply to the fiqh of the Companions during the Prophet's time because they obtained rulings directly from revelation without the need for the faculty of deduction. This passage is essential for understanding the Hanafi epistemological view of fiqh as a dynamic process of deduction rather than static knowledge.

Key Terms
مسائل قیاسیہ (masa'il qiyasiyya): Rulings that are derived through analogical reasoning (qiyas) from primary sources. They are the result of ijtihad and are not directly stated in revelation.
دور (dawr): Circular reasoning: a logical fallacy in the definition where the thing defined and what defines it depend on each other.
اجتہاد (ijtihad): The effort of a qualified jurist to derive rulings from the sources of law, using qiyas and other methods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why is the objection that later mujtahids could simply learn qiyasi issues from earlier ones invalid?
A) Because qiyasi issues change over time.
B) Because a mujtahid cannot do taqlid and must derive them himself.
C) Because later mujtahids are not qualified.
D) Because the earlier mujtahids never existed.

Key Takeaway
Qiyasi issues are the fruit of fiqh, not its root; requiring them would cause circular reasoning.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
12 min
Four Objections to the Definition of Fiqh and Their Refutations
Critique of a definition of fiqh with four objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state four objections to the definition of fiqh as 'knowledge of rulings that have appeared through revelation', explain why each undermines the definition, and identify the Hanafi position that fiqh includes analogical rulings.

Core Idea
Fiqh cannot be limited to directly revealed rulings because analogical derivation constitutes the bulk of fiqh.

The matn under commentary defines fiqh as knowledge of rulings made manifest by revelation and, if applicable, ijma. The commentator finds this definition deeply problematic and raises four objections here. The third and fourth objections are detailed: the definition would exclude analogical rulings (qiyasiyyah), and the phrase 'appearance of revelation' is ambiguous. Through careful refutation, the commentator defends a broader, operational conception of fiqh that includes ijtihad-based rulings—a key Hanafi principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target definition
Identify the exact definition of fiqh being critiqued: it is knowledge of rulings that have appeared through revelation and, if present, also those established by ijma. Understand that this definition aims to limit fiqh to directly revealed or consensus-based rulings.
This definition is from the matn; the commentator is expanding and critiquing it.
2
Analyze the third objection (qiyas exclusion)
The third objection argues that if fiqh only covers rulings manifested via revelation, then analogical rulings (qiyasiyyah) are excluded. Yet for the Hanafis, the majority of fiqh is analogical. The refutation: for the mujtahid who derives a ruling through qiyas, the revelation (the proof) has become manifest to him, so that ruling is fiqh relative to that mujtahid.
This introduces relativity: fiqh varies with the mujtahid's ijtihad.
3
Analyze the fourth objection (ambiguity of manifestation)
The fourth objection challenges the phrase 'appearance of revelation'. If it means appearance to anyone in general, then many Companions were unaware of rulings revealed to others, yet they were still considered fuqaha (e.g., they deferred to Aisha). If it means appearance to the majority, this is unregulatable due to the vast number of narrators and their dispersion. Even if accepted, it would mean that a solitary narrator's ruling is not fiqh until it becomes widespread—delaying legal knowledge.
This shows the practical impossibility of such a restrictive definition.
4
Examine the commentator's refutation and conclusion
The commentator does not propose an alternative definition but demonstrates why the given one is fraught. The Urdu translation further clarifies that a mujtahid must know the rulings of other mujtahids to avoid contradictory outcomes, and that the definition fails to account for the dynamic growth of fiqh over time.
The overall message: fiqh is a science that includes analogical reasoning and is not static.
5
Connect to the Hanafi usul position
In Hanafi usul, fiqh is defined as knowledge of practical shar'i rulings derived from detailed evidences, including qiyas and istihsan. This lesson shows why the narrower definition is rejected and why the Hanafi school includes qiyasi rulings as integral parts of fiqh.
This affirms the epistemological weight of qiyas as a source of fiqh.

الترويح لِحَلَّ التَّوْضِيحِ وَالتَّنويع
لِعَدَمِ الْإِجْمَاعِ فِى زَمَانِهِ وَكَأَنَّهُ أَرَادَ أَنَّهُ الْعِلْمُ بِمَا ظَهَرَ نُزُولُ الْوَحْيِ بِهِ فَقَطْ إِنْ لَمْ يَكُنُ إِجْمَاعٌ وَبِهِ وَبِمَا انْعَقَدَ عَلَيْهِ الْإِجْمَاعُ إِنْ كَانَ وَمِثْلُهُ فِي التَّعْرِيفَاتِ بَعِيدٌ الثَّالِثُ أَنَّهُ يَلْزَمُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْعِلْمُ بِالأحْكَامِ الْقِيَاسِيَّةِ خَارِجًا عَنْ الْفِقْهِ ، وَذَلِكَ عِندَهُمْ مُعَظَّمُ مَسَائِلِ الْفِقْهِ اللَّهُمَّ إِلَّا أَنْ يُقَالَ إِنَّهُ فِقْةٌ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَى مَنْ أَدَّى إِلَيْهِ اجَتِهَادُهُ ، إِذْ قَدْ ظَهَرَ عَلَيْهِ نُزُولُ الْوَحْيِ بِهِ وَحِينَئِذٍ يَكُونُ الْفِقْهُ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَى كُلِّ مُجْتَهد شَيْئًا آخَرَ .الرَّابِعُ أَنَّهُ إِنْ أُرِيدَ بِظُهُورِ نُزُولِ الْوَحْيِ الطُّهُورُ فِي الْجُمْلَةِ فَكَثِيرٌ مِنْ فُقَهَاءِ الصَّحَابَةِ لَمْ يَعْرِفُوا كَثِيرًا مِنْ الْأحْكَامِ الَّتِى ظَهَرَ نُزُولُ الْوَحْيِ بِهَا عَلَى بَعْضٍ الصَّحَابَةِ كَمَا رَجَعُوا فِى كَثِيرٍ مِنْ الْوَقَائِعِ إِلَى عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهَا وَلَمْ يَقْدَحُ ذَلِكَ فِي فَقَاهَتِهِمْ ، وَإِنْ أُرِيدَ الطُّهُورُ عَلَى الْأَعَمِّ الْأَغْلَبِ فَهُوَ غَيْرُ مَضْبُوطٍ لِكَثْرَةِ الرُّوَاةِ وَتَفَرُّقِهِمْ فِي الْأَسْفَارِ وَالْأَشْغَالِ وَلَوْ سُلَّمَ فَيَلْزَمُ أَنْ لَا يَكُونَ الْعِلْمُ بِالْحُكْمِ الَّذِى يَرُوِيهِ الْآحَادُ مِنَ الْفِقْهِ حَتَّى يَصِيرَ شَائِعًا ظَاهِرًا عَلَى الْأَكْثَرِ فَيَصِيرُ فِقَهَا وَبِالْجُمُلَةِ هَذَا التَّعْرِيفُ لَا يَخْلُو عَنْ الْإِشْكَالِ وَالِاخْتِلَالَ
ترجمہ :۔ یعنی شرط نہیں ہے فقہ میں مسائل قیاسیہ جاننے کی اس لئے کہ یہ فقاہت اور اجتہاد کا نتیجہ ہیں بوجہ ہونے ان کے اجتہاد سے مستنبط شدہ فروع کے پس ان کا علم موقوف ہوگا اس شخص کے فقیہ ہونے پر پس اگر فقاہت موقوف ہو ان مسائل کے جانے پر تو دور لازم آئے گا ، پس اگر اعتراض کیا جائے کہ یہ اعتراض سوائے اس کے نہیں درست ہوگا قیاس کرنے والوں میں سے پہلے شخص کے بارے میں اور وہ لوگ جو اس کے بعد میں آئے پس جائز ہے شرط لگانا اس میں ان مسائل قیاسیہ کے جاننے کی جن کو مجتہد اول نے قیاس کیا ہے بغیر دور کے لازم آنے کے تو ہم جواب میں کہیں گے جائز نہیں ہے مجتہد کے لئے تقلید کرنا بلکہ اس پر واجب ہے کہ وہ مسائل قیاسیہ کو جانے اپنے اجتہاد کے ذریعے پس اگر شرط قرار دیا جائے ان مسائل قیاسیہ کے جانے ) کو تو دور لازم آئے گا۔ ہاں شرط ہے یہ کہ وہ ( مجتہد ) جانے تمام مجتہدین کے اقوال کو مسائل قیاسینہ میں تا کہ اجتماع مرکب کی مخالفت میں واقع نہ ہو جائے۔ پس اگر یہ سوال کیا جائے کہ مسائل قیاسیہ ان احکام میں سے ہیں جن کا ظہو، نزول وجی سے ہو چکا اس لئے کہ قیاس مظہر ہے (احکام کے لئے ) نہ کہ مثبت پس شرط قرار دیا جانا چاہئے آخری مجتہد کے لئے ان کو جاننا ہم (جواب میں ) کہیں گے سوائے اس کے ظاہر ہوا ہے نزول وحی اس میں مجتہد اول کے لئے نہ کہ واقع اور نفس الامر میں اور نہ مجتہد ثانی کے پاس اور نہیں ہے اس کے لئے جائز مجتہد اول کی تقلید کرنا پس اس کے لئے شرط نہیں ہے اس کی معرفت اور ممکن ہے کہ مراد لیا جائے نزول وحی کے ظہور سے کہ وہ قیاس کے واسطہ سے نہ ہو ۔ پھر یہاں کچھ ابحاث میں پہلی بحث مقصود اس فقہ کی تعریف کرنا ہے جو قوم کے درمیان مصطلح ہے اور وہ ان کے نزدیک نام ہے مخصوص معین علم کا دوسرے علوم کی طرح اور اس پر جس کو مصنف نے ذکر کیا وہ نام ہے مفہوم کی کا جو تبدیل ہوتا رہتا ہے دنوں اور زمانوں کے اعتبار سے پس ایک دن تمام احکام کے جاننے کا نام ہوتا ہے اور دوسرے دن اس سے زائد اور زائد اور اسی طرح بڑھتا رہتا ہے نبی اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانے کے ختم ہونے تک پھر بڑھنا شروع ہوتا ہے زمانوں کے اعتبار سے اور اجماعات کے منعقد ہونے سے اور اسی طرح کم ہوتا ہے نواسخ کے اعتبار سے اور اخبار احاد کے خلاف اجماع کے منعقد ہونے سے۔
دوسری بحث یہ کہ تعریف صادق نہیں آتی صحابہ کی فقہ پر نبی علیہ السلام کے زمانے میں اس زمانہ میں اجماع کے نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے پس گویا کہ مراد لیا ( ماتن نے ) کہ وہ فقہ ان احکام کا جاننا ہے جن کا ظہور نزول وحی سے ہو گیا صرف اگر اجماع نہ ہو اور ان کو اور ان مسائل کو جن پر اجماع منعقد ہو چکا جاننا (فقہ ہے ) اگر اجماع ہو اور اس طرح (تشکیک ) تعریفات میں بعید ہے۔
تیسری بحث: تحقیق لازم آتا ہے مسائل قیاسیہ علم فقہ سے خارج ہوں حالانکہ یہ ان کے ہاں فقہ کے بڑے مسائل میں سے ہیں اللہ سے مدد مانگتے ہوئے اس کے جواب میں یوں کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ یہ فقہ ہیں نسبت کرتے ہوئے اس مجتہد کی طرف جس کا اجتہاد ان مسائل تک پہنچا اس لئے کہ ان پر نزول وحی کا کا ظہور ہو چکا اور اس وقت فقہ ہر مجتہد کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے مختلف ہوگی۔
چوتھی بحث تحقیق اگر ارادہ کیا جائے نزول وحی کے ظہور سے ظہور فی الجملہ کا پس صحابہ میں سے بہت سارے فقہاء بہت سارے احکام کو نہیں جانتے تھے جن کا ظہور بعض صحابہ پر ہو چکا تھا جیسا کہ انہوں نے رجوع کیا بہت سارے واقعات میں حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ عنہا کی طرف اور یہ مانع نہیں ہے ان کی فقاہت سے اور اگر مراد لیا جائے ظہور سے ظہور علی الاعم الاغلب (یعنی اکثر صحابہ پر نزول وحی کا ظہور ہو ) تو یہ غیر منضبط ہے راویوں کے کثیر ہونے کی وجہ سے اور ان کے سفروں میں متفرق ہونے کی وجہ سے اور کاموں میں مشغول ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اگر تسلیم کر بھی لیا جائے تو لازم آئے گا یہ کہ نہ ہو اس حکم کا علم جس
The commentary on Al-Tawdih and Al-Tanwih: due to the absence of ijmā' in his time. It is as if he meant that it is knowledge of that with which the revelation of wahi has appeared only, if there is no ijmā', and with it and with what ijmā' was established upon if there is. And the like of it in definitions is far-fetched. The third: that it necessarily follows that knowledge of analogical rulings is outside of fiqh, while for them the majority of fiqh issues are such. Except that it may be said that it is fiqh in relation to the one to whom his ijtihad leads, since the revelation of wahi has appeared to him, and then fiqh in relation to every mujtahid would be something else. The fourth: that if what is meant by the appearance of the revelation of wahi is absolute appearance [in general], then many of the jurists among the Companions did not know many of the rulings whose wahi revelation appeared to some Companions. Just as they referred many incidents to Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, and that did not impugn their juristic ability. And if what is meant is appearance in the most common way, then it is not regulated due to the large number of narrators and their dispersion in travels and occupations. Even if it is conceded, it would necessitate that knowledge of the ruling that an individual narrator relates is not fiqh until it becomes widespread and apparent to the majority, then it becomes fiqh. In summary, this definition is not free from difficulty and confusion. [Urdu translation follows]
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of the definition of fiqh as presented in the matn. The commentator raises four objections to the definition that limits fiqh to knowledge of rulings that have appeared through revelation and are supported by ijmā'. 

First objection (implied from earlier context, but here the third and fourth are detailed): The third objection is that if fiqh is defined as knowledge of rulings that have appeared through revelation, then analogical rulings (qiyāsiyyah) would be excluded from fiqh. However, the majority of fiqh issues are analogical. The commentator responds by saying that such rulings are considered fiqh for the mujtahid whose ijtihad leads to them, because for him the revelation (through the proof of qiyas) has become manifest. Thus, fiqh is relative to each mujtahid.

Fourth objection: The wording 'appearance of revelation' is ambiguous. If it means general appearance (i.e., to anyone), then many Companions were unaware of rulings revealed to other Companions, yet they were still considered jurists (e.g., they referred to Aisha). If it means appearance to the majority, this is unregulated due to the vast number of narrators and their dispersal. Even if accepted, it would mean that a ruling narrated by a solitary narrator is not fiqh until it becomes widespread—which would delay the application of fiqh.

The commentator concludes that this definition is problematic. The Urdu translation expands on these points with additional clarifications about qiyas and the necessity for a mujtahid to know the rulings of other mujtahids to avoid contradictory outcomes.

Key Terms
الفقه (al-fiqh): Knowledge of rulings that have manifested through revelation or ijmā', but the definition is criticized for excluding analogical rulings.
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical deduction to derive rulings not explicitly in revelation; considered a source of fiqh for mujtahids.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fourth objection in the passage, what is the problem with defining 'appearance of revelation' as 'appearance to the majority'?
A) It would exclude rulings known only to a few Companions.
B) It is not a regulated criterion because narrators are numerous and dispersed.
C) It would make fiqh relative to each mujtahid.
D) It would require ijma, which may not exist.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh must encompass rulings derived through qiyas and ijtihad, as the majority of fiqh issues are analogical; defining it narrowly to only directly revealed rulings is unworkable and contradicted by the practice of the Companions.

Critique of the Definition of Fiqh: Four Key Discussions
Critique of the definition of fiqh as a mutable term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four main problems in the classical definition of fiqh and explain how fiqh's scope changes over time according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Fiqh's definition is not fixed; it expands with new knowledge and contracts with abrogation.

The definition of fiqh is a foundational concept in usul al-fiqh. This passage critically examines a common definition, revealing that it is not static but evolves with revelation, consensus, and abrogation. By dissecting four key discussions, you will understand why the definition must account for temporal and methodological factors.

Guided Path
1
Understand the initial definition and its mutability
Read the first discussion to see how fiqh's meaning changes day by day, increasing until the Prophet's time and then fluctuating with consensus and abrogation.
Fiqh is not a fixed body of knowledge.
2
Analyze the second discussion on the Companions
Examine why the definition fails to cover the fiqh of the Companions during the Prophet's era due to the absence of consensus at that time.
The definition seems to require consensus for something to be called fiqh.
3
Examine the third discussion on analogical issues
Understand the challenge that analogical rulings (masail qiyasiyya) are major parts of fiqh but the definition appears to exclude them. Note the response: they are fiqh relative to the deriving mujtahid.
Analogy is a source, but the definition focuses on revelation.
4
Evaluate the fourth discussion on ambiguity of 'appearance'
Consider the two interpretations of 'appearance of revelation' (general vs. majority) and their implications. Conclude that the definition remains problematic.
The phrase is fuzzy and leads to exclusions.

وجی سے ہو چکا اس لئے کہ قیاس مظہر ہے (احکام کے لئے ) نہ کہ مثبت پس شرط قرار دیا جانا چاہئے آخری مجتہد کے لئے ان کو جاننا ہم (جواب میں ) کہیں گے سوائے اس کے ظاہر ہوا ہے نزول وحی اس میں مجتہد اول کے لئے نہ کہ واقع اور نفس الامر میں اور نہ مجتہد ثانی کے پاس اور نہیں ہے اس کے لئے جائز مجتہد اول کی تقلید کرنا پس اس کے لئے شرط نہیں ہے اس کی معرفت اور ممکن ہے کہ مراد لیا جائے نزول وحی کے ظہور سے کہ وہ قیاس کے واسطہ سے نہ ہو ۔ پھر یہاں کچھ ابحاث میں پہلی بحث مقصود اس فقہ کی تعریف کرنا ہے جو قوم کے درمیان مصطلح ہے اور وہ ان کے نزدیک نام ہے مخصوص معین علم کا دوسرے علوم کی طرح اور اس پر جس کو مصنف نے ذکر کیا وہ نام ہے مفہوم کی کا جو تبدیل ہوتا رہتا ہے دنوں اور زمانوں کے اعتبار سے پس ایک دن تمام احکام کے جاننے کا نام ہوتا ہے اور دوسرے دن اس سے زائد اور زائد اور اسی طرح بڑھتا رہتا ہے نبی اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانے کے ختم ہونے تک پھر بڑھنا شروع ہوتا ہے زمانوں کے اعتبار سے اور اجماعات کے منعقد ہونے سے اور اسی طرح کم ہوتا ہے نواسخ کے اعتبار سے اور اخبار احاد کے خلاف اجماع کے منعقد ہونے سے۔ دوسری بحث یہ کہ تعریف صادق نہیں آتی صحابہ کی فقہ پر نبی علیہ السلام کے زمانے میں اس زمانہ میں اجماع کے نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے پس گویا کہ مراد لیا ( ماتن نے ) کہ وہ فقہ ان احکام کا جاننا ہے جن کا ظہور نزول وحی سے ہو گیا صرف اگر اجماع نہ ہو اور ان کو اور ان مسائل کو جن پر اجماع منعقد ہو چکا جاننا (فقہ ہے ) اگر اجماع ہو اور اس طرح (تشکیک ) تعریفات میں بعید ہے۔ تیسری بحث: تحقیق لازم آتا ہے مسائل قیاسیہ علم فقہ سے خارج ہوں حالانکہ یہ ان کے ہاں فقہ کے بڑے مسائل میں سے ہیں اللہ سے مدد مانگتے ہوئے اس کے جواب میں یوں کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ یہ فقہ ہیں نسبت کرتے ہوئے اس مجتہد کی طرف جس کا اجتہاد ان مسائل تک پہنچا اس لئے کہ ان پر نزول وحی کا کا ظہور ہو چکا اور اس وقت فقہ ہر مجتہد کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے مختلف ہوگی۔ چوتھی بحث تحقیق اگر ارادہ کیا جائے نزول وحی کے ظہور سے ظہور فی الجملہ کا پس صحابہ میں سے بہت سارے فقہاء بہت سارے احکام کو نہیں جانتے تھے جن کا ظہور بعض صحابہ پر ہو چکا تھا جیسا کہ انہوں نے رجوع کیا بہت سارے واقعات میں حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ عنہا کی طرف اور یہ مانع نہیں ہے ان کی فقاہت سے اور اگر مراد لیا جائے ظہور سے ظہور علی الاعم الاغلب (یعنی اکثر صحابہ پر نزول وحی کا ظہور ہو ) تو یہ غیر منضبط ہے راویوں کے کثیر ہونے کی وجہ سے اور ان کے سفروں میں متفرق ہونے کی وجہ سے اور کاموں میں مشغول ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اگر تسلیم کر بھی لیا جائے تو لازم آئے گا یہ کہ نہ ہو اس حکم کا علم جس کو ایک راوی نے روایت کیا ہے فقہ سے یہاں تک کہ وہ شائع ہو جائے اکثر راویوں پر ظاہر ہو جائے پھر وہ فقہ بنے گا خلاصہ یہ کہ یہ تعریف بھی خالی از اشکال و خلل نہیں ۔
It has already become because analogy is a manifestor (of rulings) not a establisher, so it should be made a condition for the last mujtahid to know them. We (in answer) will say: except that revelation has appeared for the first mujtahid, not in reality and as it is in itself, nor does the second mujtahid have it, and it is not permissible for him to imitate the first mujtahid. So knowing it is not a condition for him. And it is possible that by the appearance of revelation is meant that it is not through analogy. Then here are some discussions. The first discussion: the purpose is to define fiqh which is terminological among the people, and it is in their view the name of a specific knowledge like other sciences. And what the author mentioned is the name of a meaning that changes with days and times. So one day it is the name of knowing all rulings, and another day it is more than that, and it increases until the end of the Prophet's (peace be upon him) time. Then it begins to increase with times and the occurrence of consensus. Similarly, it decreases with abrogators and with consensus against isolated reports. Second discussion: The definition does not apply to the fiqh of the Companions during the Prophet's time because of the absence of consensus. So it is as if the matan meant that fiqh is knowing those rulings whose appearance from revelation has occurred alone, if there is no consensus, and knowing those issues on which consensus has occurred is fiqh if there is consensus. And such skepticism in definitions is unlikely. Third discussion: It necessitates that analogical issues are excluded from the science of fiqh, whereas they are among the major issues of fiqh in their view. Seeking help from Allah, it can be answered: These are fiqh relative to the mujtahid whose ijtihad reached these issues, because the appearance of revelation has occurred upon them, and then fiqh will differ relative to each mujtahid. Fourth discussion: If by appearance of revelation is meant appearance in general, then many of the Companions were jurists but did not know many rulings whose appearance had occurred to some Companions, as they referred many incidents to Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her), and this does not prevent their juristic ability. And if by appearance is meant appearance to the majority, then this is not regulated due to the abundance of narrators, their dispersion in travels, and their engagement in tasks. Even if conceded, it would require that knowledge of a ruling narrated by a single narrator is not fiqh until it spreads and becomes apparent to most narrators, then it becomes fiqh. Summary: This definition is not free from problems and defects.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a critique of the definition of fiqh. It begins by discussing that analogy manifests rulings but does not establish them, so knowing analogical issues should not be a condition for a later mujtahid because he cannot simply imitate the first mujtahid. Then it presents four critical discussions (abahath) regarding the definition of fiqh as given by the author (Sadr al-Shariah). The first discussion notes that the definition of fiqh is relative and changes over time, increasing until the Prophet's time and then fluctuating with consensus and abrogation. The second discussion points out that the definition fails to cover the fiqh of the Companions during the Prophet's era because consensus had not yet occurred. The third discussion raises the problem of excluding analogical issues (masail qiyasiyya) from fiqh, since they are central to the discipline. The response suggests that such issues are fiqh relative to the mujtahid who derived them. The fourth discussion considers the ambiguity of the phrase 'appearance of revelation'—if it means general appearance, then many Companions were jurists despite not knowing all revealed rulings; if it means appearance to the majority, then it is unregulated and would exclude rulings known only to a few until they become widespread. The passage concludes that this definition is not free from problems.

Key Terms
فقہ (fiqh): A terminological name for a specific knowledge that changes over time; initially knowing all rulings, then expanding and contracting with consensus and abrogation.
مسائل قیاسیہ (masā’il qiyāsiyya): Rulings derived through analogy (qiyas), which are considered part of fiqh relative to the mujtahid who derived them.
اجماع (ijmā‘): Consensus of the mujtahids; its occurrence affects the scope of fiqh, either expanding or confirming rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is one major problem with defining fiqh solely in terms of 'appearance of revelation'?
A) Revelation ceased after the Prophet's death.
B) It excludes rulings derived by qiyas.
C) It overemphasizes consensus.
D) It requires ijtihad to be valid.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh's definition is relative and changes with revelation, consensus, and abrogation; a static definition fails to capture its dynamic nature.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Taftazani's Three Objections on the Definition of Fiqh
Presentation and refutation of Taftazani's objections to Sadr al-Shariah's definition of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and evaluate Taftazani's three objections to Sadr al-Shariah's definition of fiqh, and articulate the Hanafi responses using the concepts of takhsis naw'i, notoriety, and mujtahid-specific inclusion.

Core Idea
Fiqh is a type-specified science; objections assuming personal specification or static conditions miss its dynamic nature.

This passage presents a critical refinement of the definition of fiqh. Taftazani raises three objections challenging the definition's scope, historical applicability, and coverage of qiyasi issues. The Hanafi response defends the definition by clarifying the type of specification (naw'i vs. shakhsi), the notoriety of ijmah's occurrence, and the perspective-dependent inclusion of qiyasi rulings. Understanding this exchange sharpens your grasp of how usul al-fiqh defines its subject matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target definition
Recall that Sadr al-Shariah's definition of fiqh is the knowledge of practical shar'i rulings derived from detailed proofs, with conditions like ijmah formation. This is the definition under attack.
The exact definition is not quoted here, but referenced. You may need to cross-reference earlier lessons.
2
Analyze the first objection and response
Taftazani argues that fiqh is specific (makhsus) knowledge, but the definition implies it is a general concept that changes. The response distinguishes between personal specificity (takhsis shakhsi) and type specificity (takhsis naw'i). Fiqh is type-specific: the category remains while instances vary.
This resolves the apparent contradiction; change does not invalidate the definition.
3
Analyze the second objection and response
Taftazani objects that the condition 'formation of consensus' (in'iqad ijma') did not exist in the Prophet's time, excluding Companions' fiqh. The response argues this is not a doubt (tashkik) but a matter of notoriety (shahra): it is well-known that ijmah occurred after the Prophet, so the condition applies to later periods.
This preserves the definition's validity across eras.
4
Analyze the third objection and response
Taftazani claims the definition excludes issues derived by qiyas (qiyasi issues). The response states that qiyasi issues are included for the mujtahid who derives them, because for him they are already manifest from revelation. However, this leads to the implication that each mujtahid's fiqh is separate.
This acknowledges a relative, not absolute, scope.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi position
After all three responses, the definition remains intact. Fiqh is a type-specific, historically grounded, and mujtahid-relative science. The objections either misinterpret the type of specification, misunderstand temporal conditions, or ignore the perspective-dependence of derivation.
This is a classic example of critical refinement in usul al-fiqh.

ہے یہ فقہ اصطلاحی کی تعریف کے خلاف ہے کیونکہ فقہ مخصوص مسائل اور مخصوص علم کا نام ہے جیسے دوسرے علوم متعین مسائل کا نام ہیں حالانکہ ماتن کی تعریف سے سمجھ میں آتا ہے کہ فقہ ایک مفہوم کلی کا نام ہے جو زمانے کے تبدیل ہونے سے تبدیل ہوتا رہتا ہے مثلاً کم زیادہ ہوتا رہتا ہے جیسے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانہ میں وحی کے آنے سے مسائل بڑھتے رہے اور آپ کے زمانہ کے بعد اجماعات منعقد ہونے سے مسائل بڑھتے
